HD      EU Commission fines wax cartel 676 mln euros
WC     354 words
PD      1 October 2008
ET      11:43 AM
SN      Agence France Presse
SC      AFPR
LA       English
CY      Copyright Agence France-Presse, 2008 All reproduction and presentation rights reserved.

LP
The European Commission on Wednesday announced it was fining paraffin  wax producers a total of over 676 million euros (956 million dollars) for operating a price fixing  cartel which included Shell, Exxonmobil and Total.
Shell escaped any  fine under the whistle-blower rule which applies to companies which help the EU
competition authorities to uncover a  cartel.

TD
The biggest  fine of over 318 million  euros was handed out to South African company Sasol.

US giant ExxonMobil received an 83.5 million  euro fine with smaller penalties going to fellow  cartel members Repsol of Spain, Italy's ENI, Tudapetrol, Hansen and Rosenthaland and RWE of Germany, French Total and MOL of Hungary.
They were penalised for "participating in a  cartel for paraffin wax in the European Economic Area
(EEA)" between 1992 and 2005.

"Shell also participated in the  cartel but was not  fined because it revealed the existence of the  cartel to the commission," the EU executive said in a statement.
"There is probably not a household or company in  Europe that has not bought products affected by this
'paraffin  mafia' cartel, with all that implies in terms of paying over the odds, higher costs and economic
damage," said EU Competition Commissioner Neelie Kroes.

"Such illegal  cartel behaviour cannot and will not be tolerated by the  Commission, and companies' managers and shareholders should take note".

The infringement committed by ExxonMobil, Sasol, Shell, RWE and Total also related to slack  wax sold to end-customers on the German market.
Slack wax is the raw material used to produce  paraffin wax.
The fine for Sasol was increased by 50 percent "because it was the leader of the cartel," while ENI's  fine
was increased by 60 percent as it had been previously taking part in similar cartels, the commission
said.

Paraffin waxes are used in a wide variety of products such as candles,  waxed paper, paper cups and plates, the wax coating on cheese, chemicals, tyres and car components as well as in the rubber, packaging, adhesive and chewing gum industries.

HD      EU Commission fines "paraffin mafia"  cartel 676 mln euros
WC     416 words
PD      1 October 2008
ET      02:35 PM
SN      Agence France Presse
SC      AFPR
LA       English
CY      Copyright Agence France-Presse, 2008 All reproduction and presentation rights reserved.

LP
The European Commission on Wednesday announced it was fining paraffin  wax producers more than
676 million euros (956 million dollars) for operating a price fixing  cartel that included Shell, Exxonmobil
and Total.

Shell escaped a fine under the whistle-blower rule, which applies to companies that help EU competition authorities to uncover a  cartel.

TD
The biggest  fine of over 318 million  euros was handed out to South African company Sasol.

US giant ExxonMobil received an 83.5-million-euro fine with smaller penalties going to fellow  cartel members Repsol of Spain, Italy's ENI, Tudapetrol, Hansen and Rosenthaland and RWE of Germany, French Total and MOL of Hungary.
They were penalised for "participating in a  cartel for paraffin wax in the European Economic Area
(EEA)" between 1992 and 2005.

"Shell also participated in the  cartel but was not  fined because it revealed the existence of the  cartel to the commission," the EU executive said in a statement.

Paraffin waxes are used in a products ranging from candles and  waxed paper, paper cups and plates, to tyres, packaging and chewing gum.
"There is probably not a household or company in  Europe that has not bought products affected by this
'paraffin  mafia' cartel, with all that implies in terms of paying over the odds, higher costs and economic
damage," said EU Competition Commissioner Neelie Kroes.

"Such illegal  cartel behaviour cannot and will not be tolerated by the  Commission, and companies' managers and shareholders should take note."

The infringement committed by ExxonMobil, Sasol, Shell, RWE and Total also related to slack  wax sold to end-customers on the German market.
Slack wax is the raw material used to produce  paraffin wax.
The fine for Sasol was increased by 50 percent "because it was the leader of the cartel," while ENI's  fine
was increased by 60 percent as it had been previously taking part in similar cartels, the commission
said.

A spokesman for the Total group in Paris said it had received notification and was "awaiting the reasons for the decision" in order to determine what measures are necessary.

ExxonMobil was more immediately penitent, saying in a statement that it "deeply regrets its involvement, although limited, in the infringement of competition laws through the participation of a few of the company's former employees."

"Honesty, integrity, and strict legal compliance are the cornerstones of the way ExxonMobil conducts its business," the firm added.

HD     EU fines Total 128 mln euros for price-fixing
WC    239 words
PD     1 October 2008
ET     11:18 AM SN     AFX Asia SC     AFXASI LA     English
CY     (c) 2008, AFX Asia. All rights reserved.

LP
PARIS, Oct 1 (Reuters) - Total has been fined about 128 million  euros ($181 million) by the  European    Commission for fixing prices of paraffin  wax, the French oil company said on Wednesday. A Total spokeswoman said the company's French division was one of nine accused of fixing the price of the  wax used for candles and  waxed paper between 1992 and 2005. The  Commission also fined South Africa's Sasol and Italy's Eni but the spokeswoman did not specify how much. Royal Dutch Shell was not  fined, she added. The  European Commission had informed Total of its decision on Wednesday, Total said, but it had yet to receive the supporting arguments. "Total will examine the supporting arguments of the judgment and examine the means of appeal," the spokeswoman said. Total received notification in 2007
of the claim that nine companies had exchanged confidential information concerning  paraffin wax. Shares in Total, the world's fourth largest company, were little changed at 42.5  euros by 0853 GMT.

TD
(Reporting by Vanessa Walters and Benjamin Mallet; Editing by Paul Bolding) ($1=.7079  Euro) Keywords: TOTAL/ tf.TFN-Europe_newsdesk@thomson.com ak

HD     EU fines wax makers' cartel 676 mln euros

BRUSSELS, Oct 1 (Reuters) - The European Commission fined nine petrochemicals companies a total of 676 million euros ($955 million) on Wednesday for forming a "paraffin  mafia" to fix prices and carve up markets for paraffin  wax, an official statement said. The biggest individual  fine of 318.2 million  euros was imposed on Sasol of Germany and South Africa, which the  European Union executive described as the leader of the illegal  cartel. Shell escaped a  fine because it blew the whistle to the EU competition authorities. The other companies involved were ENI, Exxon Mobil , Hansen & Rosenthal, Tudapetrol,
MOL, Repsol , RWE and Total, the  Commission said.

TD
"There is probably not a household or company in  Europe that has not bought products affected by this
'paraffin  mafia'  cartel, with all that implies in terms of paying over the odds, higher costs and economic
damage," EU Competition Commissioner Neelie Kroes said in a statement. (Reporting by Paul Taylor,
editing by Dale Hudson) ($1=.7079  euro) Keywords: EU  WAX/CARTEL

HD     UPDATE 1-EU fines "paraffin mafia"  wax makers' cartel
WC    338 words
PD     1 October 2008
ET     12:09 PM SN     AFX Asia SC     AFXASI LA     English
CY     (c) 2008, AFX Asia. All rights reserved.

LP
BRUSSELS, Oct 1 (Reuters) - The European Commission fined nine petrochemicals companies a total of 676 million euros ($955 million) on Wednesday for forming a "paraffin  mafia" to fix prices and carve up markets for paraffin  wax, an official statement said. The biggest individual  fine of 318.2 million  euros was imposed on Sasol of Germany and South Africa, which the  European Union executive described as the leader of the illegal  cartel. Oil major Shell escaped a  fine because it blew the whistle to the EU
competition authorities. "There is probably not a household or company in  Europe that has not bought products affected by this 'paraffin  mafia' cartel, with all that implies in terms of paying over the odds, higher costs and economic damage," EU Competition Commissioner Neelie Kroes said in the statement. The other companies involved were ENI, Exxon Mobil , Hansen & Rosenthal, Tudapetrol, MOL, Repsol , RWE and Total, the  Commission said.

TD
It was the fourth-highest  fine ever imposed by EU regulators on a sector, topped only by the record 992.3 million euros on elevator companies last year, 790.5 million on makers of vitamins in 2001 and 750.5 million on manufacturers of gas insulated switchgear in 2007.  Paraffin waxes are used in a wide range of products from candles to paper cups and plates, the  wax coating of cheese, chemicals, tyres and chewing gum. The Commission said the cartel activity took place between 1992 and 2005, when it began investigating with raids on petrochemicals companies prompted by an application from Shell for leniency
in return for information provided. (Reporting by Paul Taylor, editing by Dale Hudson) ($1=.7079  euro) Keywords: EU  WAX/CARTEL Keywords: EU  WAX/CARTEL

HD     EU fines 9 companies over wax cartel
BY      By RAF CASERT
CR     Associated Press Writer
WC     544 words
PD      1 October 2008
ET      01:35 PM
SN      Associated Press Newswires
SC      APRS
LA      English
CY      (c) 2008. The Associated Press. All Rights Reserved.

LP
BRUSSELS, Belgium (AP) - The  European Union on Wednesday imposed one of its highest ever  cartel fines on a "paraffin  mafia" accused of fixing prices and markets for everyday household products like chewing gum, tires and candles.

A group of nine  paraffin wax producers were ordered to pay  fines totaling almost euro700 million (almost US$1 billion) for forcing  European consumers to pay more because paraffin  was kept at artificially high prices.

TD
European Commission Neelie Kroes said the  cartel leader was Sasol Ltd. of South Africa but also included such multinationals as ExxonMobil, Repsol, Shell and Total.  Paraffin wax is obtained from petroleum and is used in candles,  wax paper, cosmetics and many other products.

The overall total of euro676 million (US$967 million) is the fourth highest  fine ever and the fine slapped on Sasol of euro318.2 million ($455.12 million) was the fourth largest for an individual company.

"I hope that the harsh lesson of these high  fines will encourage the management of these companies to look very carefully at what their staff is doing," Kroes said. "And I hope that in turn the shareholders of these companies look very carefully at the management."

"They should not be under any illusion -- such illegal  cartel behavior cannot and will not be tolerated," said the commissioner, who has turned  cartel fighting into a priority issue.
The companies involved can still appeal the  fine and Sasol intends to do so.

"Sasol is surprised by and does not understand the reasons for the magnitude of this  fine and will be studying the reasons for the finding with a view to lodge an appeal against it," the company said in a statement.

"Sasol views this matter in a serious light and has intensified its competition and antitrust law compliance programs in all its businesses including joint ventures. It is Sasol's policy to comply with all applicable laws, including competition laws."
The European market for paraffin wax totals about  euro500 million (US$700 million) a year and the
cartel covered about three quarters of that for 13 years. "The 'paraffin  mafia'  cartel ran from 1992 to
2005," Kroes said.

At first, Kroes said, the companies showed a common resolve to rig the market when they started meeting secretly in Hamburg's Blauer Salon under the code name "the blue saloon group."
Meetings all over Europe followed as the  cartel flourished. But then Shell started informing the
commission about the illegal practices.
"By being the first to bring us evidence, Shell avoided a  fine of euro96 million (US$137 million)," she said.


Page 11 of 191 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
Sasol's  fine was increased by 50 percent for being the  cartel leader but the South African company also got a reduction for being the second company for cooperating with Kroes's office. Still, its  fine was one of the highest ever.
Total of France was given a  fine of euro128 million (US$183 million) and the U.S. company
ExxonMobileuro83.5 million (US$119 million).
Other companies  fined were Repsol of Spain, ENI of Italy, Tudapetrol, Hansen & Rosenthal and RWE of
Germany and MOL of Hungary.
------
Associated Press writer Celean Jacobson contributed to this report from Johannesburg, South Africa.

HD      European Union finesExxon Mobil, 8 other companies over wax cartel
BY      By RAF CASERT
CR     Associated Press Writer
WC     595 words
PD      1 October 2008
ET      09:04 PM
SN      Associated Press Newswires
SC      APRS
LA      English
CY      (c) 2008. The Associated Press. All Rights Reserved.

LP
BRUSSELS, Belgium (AP) - The European Union on Wednesday imposed one of its highest ever  cartel fines -- almost $1 billion -- on a "paraffin  mafia" accused of fixing prices and markets for everyday household products like chewing gum, tires and candles.

A group of nine  paraffin wax producers including Exxon Mobil Corp. of the United States were ordered to pay fines totaling almost 700 million  euros for forcing  European consumers to pay more because paraffin was kept at artificially high prices.

TD
European Commission Neelie Kroes said the  cartel leader was Sasol Ltd. of South Africa but also included such multinationals as Exxon Mobil, Repsol, Shell and Total.  Paraffin wax is obtained from petroleum and is used in candles,  wax paper, cosmetics and many other products.
The overall total of 676 million  euros ($967 million) is the fourth highest  fine ever and the fine slapped on
Sasol of 318.2 million  euros ($455.12 million) was the fourth largest for an individual company.

"I hope that the harsh lesson of these high  fines will encourage the management of these companies to look very carefully at what their staff is doing," Kroes said. "And I hope that in turn the shareholders of these companies look very carefully at the management."

"They should not be under any illusion -- such illegal  cartel behavior cannot and will not be tolerated," said the commissioner, who has turned  cartel fighting into a priority issue.
The companies involved can still appeal the  fine and Sasol intends to do so.

"Sasol is surprised by and does not understand the reasons for the magnitude of this  fine and will be studying the reasons for the finding with a view to lodge an appeal against it," the company said in a statement.

"Sasol views this matter in a serious light and has intensified its competition and antitrust law compliance programs in all its businesses including joint ventures. It is Sasol's policy to comply with all applicable laws, including competition laws."

Exxon Mobil, which was  fined 83.5 million euros ($119 million), was uncertain on its course of action but said earlier in a statement it "deeply regrets its involvement, although limited, in the infringement of competition laws through the participation of a few of the company's former employees."
The European market for paraffin wax totals about 500 million euros ($700 million) a year and the
cartel covered about three quarters of that for 13 years. "The 'paraffin  mafia'  cartel ran from 1992 to
2005," Kroes said.

At first, Kroes said, the companies showed a common resolve to rig the market when they started meeting secretly in Hamburg's Blauer Salon under the code name "the blue saloon group."



Page 13 of 191 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
Meetings all over Europe followed as the  cartel flourished. But then Shell started informing the
commission about the illegal practices.
"By being the first to bring us evidence, Shell avoided a  fine of 96 million euros ($137 million)," she said. Sasol's  fine was increased by 50 percent for being the  cartel leader but the South African company also
got a reduction for being the second company for cooperating with Kroes's office. Still, its  fine was one of
the highest ever.

Total of France was given a  fine of 128 million euros ($183 million). Other companies  fined were Repsol of Spain, ENI of Italy, Tudapetrol, Hansen & Rosenthal and RWE of Germany and MOL of Hungary.
------
Associated Press writer Celean Jacobson contributed to this report from Johannesburg, South Africa.

HD      European Commission fines MOL EUR 23m for participation in paraffin wax cartel
WC    230 words
PD     1 October 2008
SN     MTI - EcoNews
SC     MTIE
LA      English
CY     (c) 2008 MTI-Eco ()

LP
Budapest, October 1, 2008 (MTI-ECONEWS) - The EuropeanCommission has decided to fine Hungarian oil and gas company MOL EUR 23m for its participation in a paraffin  wax cartel, European Commissioner for Competition Policy Neelie Kroes announced on Wednesday.

MOL was one of ten companies in the cartel, which fixed prices and shared markets for the sale of paraffin wax, Ms Kroes said. The cartel covered about three-fourths of the  European paraffin wax market and operated from 1992 until 2005.

TD
The combined fine levied on all of the companies in the cartel comes to EUR 676m, the fourth-largest ever imposed by the European Commission in a cartel case, Ms Kroes said. It reflects the duration of the cartel and the size of the market -- almost EUR 500m a year, she added.

Other companies in the  cartel were South Africa's Sasol, which led the  cartel and was fined EUR 318m; France's Total, fined EUR 128m;US-based Exxon Mobil,  fined EUR 83m; Italy's ENI, fined EUR 29m; RWE of Germany, fined EUR 37m; Germany's Hansen and Rosenthal,  fined EUR 23m, Respol of Spain, fined EUR 20m; Tudapetrol of Germany,  fined EUR 12m; and the Dutch company Shell, whose  fine was lifted because it was the first to produce evidence of the  cartel.
ekh/emon

HD      European Commission fines MOL EUR 23m for participation in paraffin wax cartel - extended
WC    316 words
PD     1 October 2008
SN     MTI - EcoNews
SC     MTIE
LA      English
CY     (c) 2008 MTI-Eco ()

LP
Budapest, October 1, 2008 (MTI-ECONEWS) - The EuropeanCommission has decided to fine Hungarian oil and gas company MOL EUR 23m for its participation in a paraffin  wax cartel, European Commissioner for Competition Policy Neelie Kroes announced on Wednesday.

MOL was one of ten companies in the cartel, which fixed prices and shared markets for the sale of paraffin wax, Ms Kroes said. The cartel covered about three-fourths of the  European paraffin wax market and operated from 1992 until 2005.

TD
The combined fine levied on all of the companies in the cartel comes to EUR 676m, the fourth-largest ever imposed by the European Commission in a cartel case, Ms Kroes said. It reflects the duration of the cartel and the size of the market -- almost EUR 500m a year, she added.

Other companies in the  cartel were South Africa's Sasol, which led the  cartel and was fined EUR 318m; France's Total, fined EUR 128m;US-based Exxon Mobil,  fined EUR 83m; Italy's ENI, fined EUR 29m; RWE of Germany, fined EUR 37m; Germany's Hansen and Rosenthal,  fined EUR 23m, Respol of Spain, fined EUR 20m; Tudapetrol of Germany,  fined EUR 12m; and the Dutch company Shell, whose  fine was lifted because it was the first to produce evidence of the  cartel.

MOL said in a statement on Wednesday it regretted that, in the 90s, it had no such internal control and auditing system that could have uncovered activity of this kind. It added that its sales of  paraffin wax during the period investigated by the  Commission were carried out by an earlier purchased subsidiary. The unit was not placed under the responsibility of the parent company until later.

Paraffin wax sales account for just one-half of one percent of MOL's revenue, MOL said.

Date Announced: 20081001

Reuters reported that The European Commission fined nine petrochemicals companies a total of EUR676 million ($955 million) for forming a paraffin  mafia to fix prices and carve up markets for paraffin  wax. Sasol Limited was  fined EUR318.2 million and Royal Dutch Shell escaped a potential fine of EUR96 million because it blew the whistle first to the EU competition authorities. The other companies fined were Total (EUR128.1 million), Exxon Mobil (EUR83.6 million, RWE (EUR37.4 million), ENI (EUR29 million), Hansen & Rosenthal (EUR24 million), MOL (EUR23.7 million), Repsol
(EUR19.8 million), and Tudapetrol (EUR12 million). The  Commission said the cartel activity took place between 1992 and 2005, when it began investigating with raids on petrochemicals companies prompted by an application from Shell for leniency in return for information provided.

HD          'PARAFFIN MAFIA' FINED £535m
BY          By Geoff Meade, PA  Europe editor, Brussels
WC         464 words
PD          1 October 2008
ET          05:51 PM
SN          Press Association National Newswire
SC          PRESSA
LA           English
CY          (c)2008, The Press Association, All Rights Reserved

LP
The European Commission today imposed fines of £535 million on what Brussels described as
Europe's "paraffin  mafia".

Ten groups of companies, including ExxonMobil, Total, Resol, Sasol and Shell, were involved in an illegal paraffin wax scam, operating a  price-fixing, market-rigging  cartel which ran for 13 years until
2005.

TD
Shell alone escaped fines under Commission "leniency" provisions, because the company revealed the existence of the cartel and claimed immunity.

EU Competition Commissioner Neelie Kroes told a press conference in Brussels: "There is probably not a household or company in  Europe that has not bought products affected by this 'paraffin  mafia' cartel, with all that implies in terms of paying over the odds, higher costs and economic damage.

"Such illegal  cartel behaviour cannot and will not be tolerated by the  Commission, and companies' managers and shareholders should take note."

Paraffin waxes are used in candles,  waxed paper, paper cups and plates and the  wax coating on cheese, as well as in chemicals, tyres and car components and in the rubber, packaging, adhesive and chewing gum industries.

The Commission investigation started with surprise inspections in April 2005, prompted by an application for immunity lodged by Shell under the EU's 2002 "Leniency Notice".

According to the  Commission the cartel was known in the Shell group as the "paraffin  mafia" and in the Sasol group as "Blauer Salon" - after the "blue saloon" hotel bar in Germany where the first meetings of the  cartel took place in 1992 to fix prices and markets between them.

Other cartel meetings took place at a series of top hotels all over  Europe, including Milan, Vienna, Budapest, Paris, Munich and Strasbourg.

The nine groups fined today were ENI, ExxonMobil, Hansen & Rosenthal, Tudapetrol, MOL, Repsol, Sasol, RWE and Total.

Along with Shell, they took part in regular gatherings to discuss prices, allocate markets and customers, and to exchange sensitive commercial information, said Ms Kroes.
She said the  cartel's activities were "a very serious infringement of EU Treaty anti-trust rules". end
(reopens)
ExxonMobil this afternoon expressed regret at the company's "limited" involvement in the  cartel.



Page 24 of 191 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
A statement said "a few" of the firm's former employees had participated in activities which infringed competition laws.

"It is ExxonMobil's policy to uphold the highest ethical standards and to comply with all applicable competition laws," said a company statement.

"ExxonMobil has a very strong competition law compliance programme and it expects its employees to observe high ethical standards.

"Honesty, integrity and strict legal compliance are the corner stones of the way ExxonMobil conducts its business.

"Frequent training and regular reviews of the company's business activities are conducted to ensure ongoing compliance with these policies and laws."
end

HD     Sasol Limited: Statement Issued by Sasol Limited  in Response to an Announcement by the
European Commission
WC    826 words
PD     1 October 2008
ET      02:09 PM
SN     PR Newswire (U.S.)
SC     PRN
LA      English
CY     Copyright © 2008 PR Newswire Association LLC. All Rights Reserved.

LP
JOHANNESBURG, South Africa, Oct. 1 /PRNewswire-FirstCall/ -- Statement issued by Sasol Limited (JSE: SOL; NYSE: SSL) in response to an announcement by the European Commission regarding a finding of anti-competitive behaviour by Sasol  Wax GmbH and other members of the European paraffin wax industry. As anticipated in several previous announcements made by Sasol Limited, the European Union found that members of the European paraffin  wax industry, including Sasol Wax GmbH, formed a cartel and violated antitrust laws. A fine of EUR 318 200 000 was imposed by the European Commission on Sasol Wax GmbH (of which Sasol  Wax International AG, Sasol Holding in Germany GmbH and Sasol Limited would be jointly and severally be liable for EUR 250 million). The  fine is payable within three months.

TD
As a result of Sasol's co-operation and support in the investigations, the  European Commission reduced the base amount of the  fine by 50% to the net amount stated above. Sasol is surprised by and does not understand the reasons for the magnitude of this  fine and will be studying the reasons for the finding with
a view to lodge an appeal against it. According to the statement of objections of the  European                  Commission an infringement of antitrust laws commenced in 1992 or even earlier. In 1995 Sasol became a co-shareholder in an existing  wax business located in Hamburg, Germany owned by the Schumann group. In July 2002 Sasol acquired the remaining shares in the joint venture and became the sole shareholder of the business. Sasol Limited was unaware of these infringements before the  European      Commission commenced their investigation at the  wax business in Hamburg in April 2005. Sasol views this matter in a serious light and has intensified its competition and anti-trust law compliance programmes in all its businesses including joint ventures. It is Sasol's policy to comply with all applicable laws,
including competition laws.

Tel.: +27 11 441 3113 / 3563 / 3321 investor.relations@sasol.com

Sasol is an integrated oil and gas company with substantial chemical interests. Based in South Africa and operating worldwide, Sasol is listed on the NYSE and JSE stock exchanges. We are the leading provider of liquid fuels in South Africa and a major international producer of chemicals. Sasol uses proprietary Fischer-Tropsch technologies for the commercial production of synthetic fuels and chemicals from
low-grade coal and natural gas. We manufacture more than 200 fuel and chemical products that are sold worldwide. In South Africa we also operate coal mines to provide feedstock for our synthetic fuels plants. Sasol operates the only inland crude oil refinery in South Africa. The group produces crude oil in offshore Gabon, supplies Mozambican natural gas to end-user customers and petrochemical plants in South Africa, and with partners involved in gas-to-liquids fuel joint ventures in Qatar and Nigeria. HD         EU Fines Wax Producers EUR676M For Price Fixing
WC        148 words

BRUSSELS (Dow Jones)--The European Commission Wednesday fined nine wax producers a total of EUR676 million for participating in a paraffin  wax cartel.

The nine producers are Sasol Ltd. (SOL.JO), ExxonMobil Corp. (XOM), ENI S.P.A (ENI.MI), Hansen & Rosenthal, Tudapetrol, MOL, Repsol, RWE and Total S.A. (12027.FR).

TD
Sasol, a South African energy company, was the leader of the  cartel and will have to pay EUR318 million, the  commission said. Total will have to pay the second largest part of the  fine at EUR128 million.
"There is probably not a household or company in Europe that hasn't bought products affected by this
'paraffin  mafia' cartel," said Neelie Kroes, the commission's antitrust chief, in a statement.
-By Matthew Dalton, Dow Jones Newswires; 32 2741 1487; matthew.dalton@dowjones.com [ 01-10-08

BRUSSELS (Dow Jones)--The European Commission Wednesday fined nine wax producers a total of EUR676 million for participating in a paraffin  wax cartel.

TD
The companies fined are Sasol Ltd. (SOL.JO), ExxonMobil Corp. (XOM), ENI SpA (ENI.MI), Hansen & Rosenthal, Tudapetrol, MOL Nyrt (MOL.BU), Repsol SA (REP), RWE AG (RWE.XE) and Total SA. (12027.FR).

1992 to 2005, and thus managed to avoid all fines, the commission said. Shell's shareholders are
lucky the company was the first to own up to the cartel, the European antitrust commissioner Neelie
Kroes said. "As it has been involved in  cartel activity before, it would have had its  fine increased by

'paraffin  mafia'  cartel," Kroes said.

Paraffin wax is used in a wide range of products - from candles and paper cups to tires and car components.

The cartel covered about 75% of the European market for paraffin wax, which is worth some EUR500 million annually, according to the commission.

ExxonMobil, which was fined EUR83 million for participating in the  cartel, said it "deeply regrets its involvement," in the cartel by few of the company's former employees, saying it would now determine whether it would need to take any further action.

HD       H&R WASAG AG: European Commission Imposes Fine On H&R WASAG WC      255 words
PD       1 October 2008
ET        03:20 PM
SN       Dow Jones International News
SC       DJI
LA        English
CY       (c) 2008 Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP
Edited Press Release
FRANKFURT (Dow Jones)--The  European Commission Wednesday said that as part of a total
financial penalty of EUR600 million against all the parties involved in the alleged  cartel, it has imposed a
fine of altogether EUR36 million on companies of the Hansen & Rosenthal Group and H&R WASAG AG
for anti-competitive behaviour in the  paraffin  sector during the years 1994 - 2005.

TD
Of the total amount, H&R Chemisch-Pharmazeutische Spezialitaeten GmbH, a subsidiary of H&R WASAG AG, is being ordered to pay a sum of EUR22 million, with sales partners a further  fine of EUR14 million. The written substantiation for the  fines has not yet been issued.

The board of H&R WASAG AG sees grounds for substantial legal objections, which already applied to the investigation proceedings. This is also reflected in the balance sheet treatment of the matter as a contingent risk. Appropriate procedural steps will be instituted against the  fine once the written substantiation has been received. Only when this is available will it be possible to form a conclusive opinion concerning the justification for the  fine and any impact it may have on the balance sheet and profit and loss account. As matters stand Wednesday, the company continues to view the  fine as unjustified in terms of both substance and amount and will on all accounts institute legal proceedings against the  Commission's decision. [ 01-10-08 1320GMT ]

HD        2nd UPDATE: EU Fines Wax Producers EUR676M For Price Fixing
WC        474 words
PD         1 October 2008
ET         04:24 PM
SN         Dow Jones International News
SC         DJI
LA         English
CY         (c) 2008 Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP
(Adds detail, background.)

BRUSSELS (Dow Jones)--The European Commission Wednesday fined nine wax producers a total of EUR676 million for participating in a paraffin  wax cartel.

TD
The companies fined include Sasol Ltd. (SOL.JO), ExxonMobil Corp. (XOM), ENI SpA (ENI.MI), Hansen & Rosenthal, Tudapetrol, MOL Nyrt (MOL.BU), Repsol SA (REP), RWE AG (RWE.XE) and Total SA. (12027.FR).
The fine is the fourth largest the  commission has ever imposed in a cartel case.

Sasol, a South African energy company, was the leader of the  cartel and will have to pay the largest part of the  fine, EUR318 million, the  commission said. Total will have to pay the second largest part of the fine of EUR128 million.
Royal Dutch Shell (RDSA) reported the praffin wax cartel, which operated for 13 years from 1992 to
2005, and thus managed to avoid all fines, the commission said. Shell's shareholders are lucky the
company was the first to own up to the cartel, the European antitrust commissioner Neelie Kroes said.
"As it has been involved in  cartel activity before, it would have had its  fine increased by 60%,"
amounting to a  fine of EUR96 million, Kroes added.

Italian oil and gas company ENI had its  fine increased by 60% to EUR29 million because it is a repeat cartel offender, having participation in the PVC and polypropylene cartels in the 1990s and 1980s, the commission said.
"There is probably not a household or company in  Europe that hasn't bought products affected by this
'paraffin  mafia' cartel," Kroes said.

Paraffin wax is used in a wide range of products - from candles and paper cups to tires and car components.

The cartel covered about 75% of the European market for paraffin wax, which is worth some EUR500 million annually, according to the commission.

ExxonMobil, which was fined EUR83 million for participating in the  cartel, said it "deeply regrets its involvement," in the cartel by few of the company's former employees, saying it would now determine whether it would need to take any further action.

Spanish Repsol faces a EUR19.8 million  fine, while German Tudapetrol is fined EUR12 million. Another German company Hansen & Rosenthal will pay a EUR24 million fine, while RWE pays EUR37.4 million, Hungarian energy company MOL was  fined EUR23.7 million.

Under Kroes' leadership the  commission has made fighting cartels one of its main priorities, with the competition chief keen to demonstrate how  cartel-busting affects  European consumers.

During the past four years, the  commission imposed more than EUR7 billion in cartel fines. This amount is likely to increase steeply after the  commission introduced harsher fines from early 2007.

BRUSSELS (Dow Jones)--The European Commission on Wednesday fined nine wax producers a total of EUR676 million for participating in a paraffin  wax cartel.

HD     Sasol Limited's response  to finding by European Commission
WC    574 words
PD     1 October 2008
SN     ENP Newswire
SC     ENPNEW
LA      English
CY     (c) 2008, Electronic News Publishing. All Rights Reserved.

LP
Release date - 01102008

Statement issued by Sasol Limited in response to an announcement by the  European Commission regarding a finding of anti-competitive behaviour by Sasol  Wax GmbH and other members of the European paraffin wax industry.

TD
As anticipated in several previous announcements made by Sasol Limited, the  European Union found that members of the European paraffin  wax industry, including Sasol Wax GmbH, formed a cartel and violated antitrust laws. A fine of EUR 318 200 000 was imposed by the European Commission on Sasol Wax GmbH (of which Sasol Wax International AG, Sasol Holding in Germany GmbH and Sasol Limited would be jointly and severally be liable for EUR 250 million). The  fine is payable within three months.

As a result of Sasol's co-operation and support in the investigations, the  European Commission reduced the base amount of the  fine by 50% to the net amount stated above.

Sasol is surprised by and does not understand the reasons for the magnitude of this  fine and will be studying the reasons for the finding with a view to lodge an appeal against it.

According to the statement of objections of the  European Commission an infringement of antitrust laws commenced in 1992 or even earlier. In 1995 Sasol became a co-shareholder in an existing  wax business located in Hamburg, Germany owned by the Schumann group. In July 2002 Sasol acquired the remaining shares in the joint venture and became the sole shareholder of the business. Sasol Limited was unaware of these infringements before the  European Commission commenced their investigation at the  wax business in Hamburg in April 2005.

Sasol views this matter in a serious light and has intensified its competition and anti-trust law compliance programmes in all its businesses including joint ventures. It is Sasol's policy to comply with all applicable laws, including competition laws.

Sasol may, in this document, make statements that are not historical facts and relate to analyses and other information based on forecasts of future results and estimates of amounts not yet determinable. These are forward-looking statements as defined in the U.S. Private Securities Litigation Reform Act of

HD     SASOL FINED BY EUROPEAN COMMISSION WC     305 words
PD      1 October 2008
SN      SAPA (South African Press Association)
SC      SAPA
LA      English
CY      (c) 2008 All copy held by SAPA, no republication without permission from SAPA

LP
South African chemical giant Sasol was  fined 318.2m Euros (R3.7bn) by the  European Commission
(EC ) after it had been found guilty of anti-competitive behaviour.
A press release issued by the EC on Tuesday revealed that nine companies involved in manufacturing
paraffin wax had been fined a total of 676  euros.

TD
Competition Commissioner Neelie Kroes said "There is probably not a household or company in  Europe that has not bought products affected by this  paraffin  mafia cartel. Such illegal  cartel behaviour cannot and will not be tolerated by the  Commission, and companies' managers and shareholders should take note".

Paraffin waxes are used in a wide variety of products such as candles,  waxed paper, paper cups and plates, the wax coating on cheese, chemicals, tyres and car components as well as in the rubber, packaging, adhesive and chewing gum industries.
In its statement, the EC said that Sasol had carried nearly 50 percent of the  fine because it was the  cartel
leader.
The cartel operated from 1992 to 2005.

Anglo-Dutch giant Shell had participated in participated in the  cartel, but its 96m  euro fine was written off because it had informed the Commision of the  cartel.
Sasol's  fine is payable within three months.

In a statement Sasol group communications manager Jacqui O'Sullivan said: "Sasol is surprised by and does not understand the reasons for the magnitude of this  fine and will be studying the reasons for the finding with a view to lodge an appeal against it."

She said Sasol Limited had bought into an existing business and it had only became the sole shareholder in the business in 2002.

"Sasol Limited was unaware of these infringements before the  European Commission commenced their investigation at the  wax business in Hamburg in April 2005."
Sapa

EU investigation.

HD     DGAP-Adhoc: H&R WASAG AG: European Commission imposes  fine on H&R WASAG WC    416 words
PD     1 October 2008
ET      03:16 PM SN     Dow Jones SC     VWDUNT LA      German
CY     Copyright 2008 Dow Jones News GmbH. All Rights Reserved

TD
H&R WASAG AG / Legal Matter

01.10.2008

Release of an Ad hoc announcement according to § 15 WpHG, transmitted by DGAP
- a company of EquityStory AG.
The issuer is solely responsible for the content of this announcement.
=-------------------------------------------------------------------------- Salzbergen, 1.10.2008
The European  Commission has today announced that as part of a total
financial penalty of EUR 600 million against all the parties involved in the alleged cartel, it has imposed a fine of altogether EUR 36 million on companies of the Hansen & Rosenthal Group and H&R WASAG AG for
anti-competitive behaviour in the paraffin sector during the years 1994 -
2005. Of the total amount, H&R Chemisch-Pharmazeutische Spezialitäten GmbH, a subsidiary of H&R WASAG AG, is being ordered to pay a sum of EUR 22 million, with sales partners a further of EUR 14 million. The written substantiation for the fines has not yet been issued.

The board of H&R WASAG AG sees grounds for substantial legal objections, which already applied to the investigation proceedings. This is also reflected in the balance sheet treatment of the matter as a contingent
risk. Appropriate procedural steps will be instituted against the fine once the written substantiation has been received. Only when this is available will it be possible to form a conclusive opinion concerning the justification for the fine and any impact it may have on the balance sheet and profit and loss account. As matters stand today, the company continues to view the fine as unjustified in terms of both substance and amount and will on all accounts institute legal proceedings against the Commission's decision.

H&R WASAG AG

Christian Pokropp

HD          EC fines paraffin wax cartel including RWE with EUR 676m

(ADP News) - Oct 1, 2008 - The European Commission (EC) said today it has imposed a EUR 676 million (USD 955.7m)  fine on an illegal paraffin  wax price cartel including German utility RWE (FSE:RWE).

RWE will have to pay EUR 37.44 million of the total sum, while Tudapetrol was  fined with EUR 12 million and Hansen&Rosenthal -- with EUR 24 million. The latter two companies are subsidiaries of local specialty chemicals group H&R Wasag AG (FSE:WAS).

TD
The other firms involved in the  cartel are South African Sasol, French Total SA, Spanish Repsol-YPF
and US ExxonMobil.
(EUR 1.0=USD 1.414) Source: (TN/IE/TN)

HD   Interfax Hungary Business Daily

BUDAPEST. OCTOBER 1. INTERFAX CENTRAL  EUROPE – Hungary's state asset manager MNV will announce a one-round public tender for the sale of properties belonging to a former military air base near southwest Hungary's Taszar, MNV announced Wednesday.

The Taszar facility served as a NATO base during the Balkans conflicts of the 1990s, but was closed down in 2005, and is currently without an airport license.

TD
Earlier this year, MNV already fielded the opinion of potential investors, receiving 12 concept applications that have influenced the content of the upcoming tender. Among others, MNV said that potential applicants preferred the sale of the property, rather than a lease scheme, and saw possibilities to develop an intermodal logistics base, in addition to what would primarily be a cargo airport.

MNV said the offered purchase price will weigh 26% toward applicants' final score, with financial strength, guarantees and the quality of development concepts each weighing a further 17%, among others.
According to press reports, the government expects developments totaling HUF 30 bln at Taszar. BUDAPEST. OCTOBER 1. INTERFAX CENTRAL  EUROPE – Hungarian property developer Gestor and
Belgium's BPI have teamed up to build a EUR 45 mln mixed project in the ninth district of Hungarian capital
Budapest, to be completed by mid-2010, the companies announced on Wednesday.

The project will involve the renovation and expansion of an old factory and warehouse building, which in recent years served as an alternative cultural center under the name Tuzraktar. The new project, named The Gallery, will build a three-star business hotel with 105 rooms, retail space totaling 2,500 square meters (sqm), and 'A' class offices with net leasable area of 10,500 sqm.

"There is a large supply of new offices in Budapest [...] but so far this has been limited to the Southern Buda and Southern Pest areas of the city, and the Vaci Ut office corridor," Gestor CEO Andras Gero was quoted saying. "At the same time, there is a lack of quality projects along the road leading to the Ferihegy international airport [where The Gallery will be located]."

With 200 underground parking places and a pedestrian passage, total built-in space in The Gallery will reach 29,500 sqm.

Gestor, owned by private investor Peter Gero and his family, has ongoing projects worth a total HUF 20 bln in Hungary, mostly in the residential segment. The group, founded in 1990, is also active in facility management and property consulting.
BPI is part of Belgium's CFE group, a construction, real estate and infrastructure conglomerate active in the
Benelux countries, Hungary, Poland and Slovakia.

BUDAPEST. OCTOBER 1. INTERFAX CENTRAL EUROPE – Hungary's top oil and gas company MOL has received a EUR 23 mln fine from the European Commission (EC), as part of a  cartel investigation involving the EU's paraffin  wax market that led to fines totaling EUR 676 mln.

"The cartel covered about 75% of the European market in paraffin wax, lasted for 13 years, and included
10 companies," Neelie Kroes, European Commissioner for Competition Policy announced in Brussels
Wednesday. "The companies have been  fined a total of EUR 676 mln, the fourth largest  fine ever imposed
by the EC in a  cartel case, [reflecting] both the long duration of the  cartel and the size of the market
concerned – nearly EUR 500 mln a year."
Page 46 of 191 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
Kroes said the  paraffin  mafia cartel ran from 1992 to 2005. In the beginning, the  cartel met at the Blauer Salon, a hotel bar in Hamburg, Germany.  Cartel meetings subsequently took place at a series of top hotels all over Europe – Milan, Vienna, Budapest, Paris, Munich, Strasbourg and others, according to the Commissioner.

German-South African manufacturer Sasol was the leader of the  cartel, and was rewarded with a EUR 318 mln fine. France's Total received a EUR 128 mln  fine, while U.S.-based Exxon Mobil will have to pay a
EUR 83 mln penalty. Other companies involved in the  cartel – including MOL – were awarded  fines
between EUR 12–37 mln each.
U.K.-based oil major Shell, which blew the whistle on the  cartel, has escaped what would have been a
EUR 96 mln fine, Kroes added.

Paraffin wax is used in a wide range of products – tyres, car components,  waxed paper, paper cups and plates, packaging, adhesive, candles, chewing gum, and the  wax coating on cheese, among others.

BUDAPEST. OCTOBER 1. INTERFAX CENTRAL  EUROPE – Holcim Hungaria Zrt, the Hungarian unit of Swiss cement maker Holcim, has received a construction permit for its planned EUR 300-mln new cement factory in northern Hungary's Nyergesujfalu, the company announced in a statement.

"Securing the construction permit is a significant step for us," chairman-CEO Richard Skene was quoted saying. "We are convinced that remaining preparatory measures can be completed soon."

Holcim said earlier it will employ 280 workers in the Nyergesujfalu factory, once production starts in 2010. Of these, 228 will be transferred from Holcim's other factory in nearby Labatlan, which will be closed down following the new factory's completion.

Before the launch of construction, Holcim still needs to finalize agreements with subcontractors, and take additional steps to prepare the site for building.

The new cement factory will have annual capacity of 1.77 mln tonnes. Preparations to build the factory began in 2005.

BUDAPEST. OCTOBER 1. INTERFAX CENTRAL  EUROPE – Hungarian developer Biggeorge's-NV is ready to launch construction of a HUF 20–25 bln airport near the Hungarian city of Szekesfehervar 60 kilometers west of the capital Budapest, in the first part of 2009, Robert Stalmayer, the director of the project company, told Interfax.

"After a long procedure to get the permits, which took nearly four years, we now have all necessary authorizations to start the HUF 20–25 bln investment in the first part of 2009," Stalmayer said.

The development, to be named Alba Airport, will open for business at the start of the summer season in March 2010. The project company, Alba Airport Kft, is currently 50% owned by Biggeorge's-NV and 25% each by the local governments of Szekesfehervar and the neighboring town of Aba. However, Biggeorge's-NV's share will soon increase to 90% while the municipalities will own a total of 10%.

Stalmayer said the airport will be built on a 180-hectare plot on a run-down former military air base, owned by the local governments but leased to Alba Airport for a period of 60 years.

Stalmayer could not yet provide details of the financing plan of the project, but noted that Alba Airport expects to involve outside investors as well.

"We are in the process of finding other investors, such as property developers or professional investors, and although the credit crunch will surely impede this process, this project is good enough to attract other companies," Stalmayer noted.

The company sees Alba Airport as possibly the first genuine rival to Hungary's main international airport, Ferihegy near Budapest. While Ferihegy handles more than eight million passengers a year, most small regional airports in Hungary have rarely managed beyond a few tens of thousands of passengers a year.

"We expect to already have 150,000 passengers in 2010, while the capacity of the airport is eventually seen to be expanded to two million," Stalmayer said, noting that he expects to reach one million passengers by the fifth year of operation.

Stalmayer said that although the airport initially plans to serve low-cost airlines and charter flights, the facility will be able to accommodate traditional airlines as well.

Stalmayer noted that he is optimistic regarding the airport's growth potential because of its advantageous location, close to major tourist destinations Budapest, lake Balaton and lake Velencei, which are seen
Page 47 of 191 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
attracting a sizable influx of foreign tourists. Meanwhile, plans to create direct bus and train services to the airport are aimed at maximizing the airport's domestic catchment area.

"The airport can be reached in a 90-minute drive by 3.5 million potential passengers, and this is essential in order to bring a discount airline base here," Stalmayer said.

He added that a low-cost airline base is expected to be opened at Alba Airport by the third or fourth year of operation.

In addition to creating new jobs locally, Alba Airport is also seen boosting the regional economy, by increasing tourist activity as well as bringing in industries that involve significant moves in personnel, such as the automotive and pharmaceutical industries.

Stalmayer noted that the company also plans to set up an industrial park on a 110-hectare plot near the airport, which is expected to attract additional passengers to the airport.

BUDAPEST. OCTOBER 1. INTERFAX CENTRAL  EUROPE – ECONOMY: Researcher Forecasts 3% GDP Growth in 2009 – According to the latest forecasts released by economic research institute GKI, revised in light of global finance market developments, Hungary's GDP will grow 3% in 2009, while the national economy will resume a slow but steady growth trajectory. Private consumption would increase 2.5%, investments 10%, while exports and imports would increase 12% with inflation dropping to 4.2%, GKI said. [Nepszava]

AGRICULTURE: Hungary, Poland Submit Joint Proposal to Aid Apple Farmers – Hungary and Poland have jointly submitted a request to the EU for support to apple farmers struggling with low wholesale prices and
a cap on cheap Chinese imports, Hungarian Agriculture Minister Jozsef Graf said. The countries would require EUR 2,000–3,000 per hectare in order to reduce the sizes of apple orchards, which cannot be profitably cultivated. [Napi Gazdasag]

LABOR: Prison Economy Generates Turnover of HUF 6.8 bln in 2008 – The twelve state-owned companies involved in the employment of convicted criminals reported an aggregate turnover of HUF 6.8 bln in 2008, meaning the companies completed another profitable year despite the global economic downturn.
Currently, 6,700 convicts work, who cost a total of HUF 400 mln in labor expenses and an additional HUF
150 mln for training. The expenses are far outweighed by the collected profits, involved companies said.
[Napi Gazdasag]

DEFENSE: Hungarian Military Takes Control of Kabul International Airport – As of October 1, the Hungarian military is to take control of the Kabul international airport in Afghanistan. Hungarian soldiers and experts will be responsible for controlling air traffic, safety provisions and logistics, while the premises will continue to be guarded by the U.S. army. The Hungarian Defense Ministry did not wish to comment on the takeover of control, saying officials would release a statement later in the day. [Magyar Hirlap]

CURRENT AFFAIRS: One Third of Hungarians Strongly Prejudiced against Foreigners – Study – According to a regular survey prepared by pollster Tarki on Hungarian's general attitude towards
foreigners, the last year has brought no major changes. One third of the population would keep the nation's borders hermetically sealed, some 10% are pro-foreigners while the largest group, 58% of the total population would contemplate allowing entry based on the applicant's nationality.

An interesting element in the study is measuring the general attitude towards "Piresians," citizens of a non-existent country created by researchers. Rejection of the fictitious ethnicity has not changed much
from last year's 68%, since 66% of all Hungarians would still not allow them to enter the country, Tarki said. [Nepszabadsag]
BUDAPEST. OCTOBER 1. INTERFAX CENTRAL  EUROPE – REAL ESTATE: Government Expects HUF
30-bln Investments at Former Military Airbase – The government is expecting a HUF 30 bln investment and
a HUF 10–15-bln airport development total from the single-round privatization of the Taszar military airbase
in southwestern Hungary, said government commissioner Istvan Kolbert. The state should have little
trouble finding a new owner, since 12 businesses indicating they would be willing to post a bid in the
procedure that officially opnes on October 1, Kolber added. [Vilaggazdasag]

ENERGY: Institutional Investors Accept MOL Bid for Croatian Energy Firm – Institutional investors of Croatian energy company INA have accepted the HRK 2,800 per share purchase offer by Hungarian oil and gas company MOL, aimed at taking over the 31% package of publicly traded INA papers. However, it is uncertain how much of their respective stakes the investors are willing to sell. [Nepszava, Napi Gazdasag]

The new funds will allow the company to improve services in its network, CEO Peter Csicsaky said. [Nepszava, Napi Gazdasag]

major role in developing the country's northern areas, said deputy CEO Bernadett Tatrai. The bank is set to continue expansion, since its H1 business figures indicate that new openings so far have contributed
greatly to overall performance, Tatrai said. [Nepszava]
CAR INDUSTRY: Delphi Forced to Shut Down Production Line Upon Lapse in Orders –
Szombathely-based (western Hungary) electronics company Delphi Hungary Kft was forced to shut down
one of its production lines upon the major lapse in automotive industry orders seen over the past weeks,
said company executive Karl Aschemann. To date, no lay-offs were made necessary, since the workers at
the deactivated production division were reassigned to other departments in the company, Aschemann
said. [Napi Gazdasag]

MEDIA: Comedy Central Begins Hungarian Broadcast – October 1 marks the launch of the Hungarian Comedy Central television channel, the local version of the popular U.S. comedy-themed station. BUDAPEST. OCTOBER 1. INTERFAX CENTRAL  EUROPE – The Hungarian forint continued to ease against major currencies on Wednesday as the market confidently awaits the U.S. Senate's decision later on Wednesday on the banking sector bailout bill.

The Hungarian forint opened weaker than Tuesday's closing mark, and although it firmed later in the morning, it lost ground again after the publication of poor EU and U.S. employment data in the afternoon and closed at EUR/HUF 242.53, which compares to late Tuesday's EUR/HUF 241.36.
The forint-U.S. dollar pair traded in a similar path and closed at USD/HUF 172.80, which compares to
Tuesday's USD/HUF 171.73.

Fixed-income yields were down on Wednesday, falling 2-14 basis points across the board, according to data provided by the Government Debt Management Agency (AKK).

Analysts expect forint trading in coming days to be influenced by the outcome of the U.S. Senate vote later in the evening.

"Markets are set to lack domestic driving factors, with all eyes remaining on the global market sentiment, including the fate of the U.S. bailout package," CIB Bank analysts said in a Wednesday note.

BUDAPEST. OCTOBER 1. INTERFAX CENTRAL EUROPE - Hungary's top oil and gas company MOL has received a EUR 23 mln fine from the European Commission (EC), as part of a  cartel investigation involving the EU's paraffin  wax market that led to fines totaling EUR 676 mln.

"The cartel covered about 75% of the European market in paraffin wax, lasted for 13 years, and included 10 companies," Neelie Kroes, European Commissioner for Competition Policy announced in Brussels Wednesday. "The companies have been  fined a total of EUR 676 mln, the fourth largest  fine ever imposed by the EC in a  cartel case, [reflecting] both the long duration of the  cartel and the size of the market concerned - nearly EUR 500 mln a year."

TD
Kroes said the  paraffin  mafia cartel ran from 1992 to 2005. In the beginning, the  cartel met at the Blauer Salon, a hotel bar in Hamburg, Germany.  Cartel meetings subsequently took place at a series of top hotels all over  Europe - Milan, Vienna, Budapest, Paris, Munich, Strasbourg and others, according to the Commissioner.
German-South African manufacturer Sasol was the leader of the  cartel, and was rewarded with a EUR
318 mln fine. France's Total received a EUR 128 mln  fine, while U.S.-based Exxon Mobil will have to
pay a EUR 83 mln penalty. Other companies involved in the  cartel - including MOL - were awarded
fines between EUR 12-37 mln each.
U.K.-based oil major Shell, which blew the whistle on the  cartel, has escaped what would have been a
EUR 96 mln fine, Kroes added.

Paraffin wax is used in a wide range of products - tyres, car components,  waxed paper, paper cups and plates, packaging, adhesive, candles, chewing gum, and the  wax coating on cheese, among others.
BS/PS

Sasol Limited

("Sasol" or "the Company")

Statement issued by Sasol Limited in response to an announcement by the

European  Commission regarding a finding of anti-competitive behaviour by
Sasol
Wax GmbH and other members of the European  paraffin  wax industry

As anticipated in several previous announcements made by Sasol Limited, the

European Union found that members of the European  paraffin  wax industry, including Sasol Wax GmbH, formed a cartel and violated antitrust laws. A fine of EUR 318 200 000 was imposed by the European  Commission on Sasol Wax GmbH (of which Sasol Wax International AG, Sasol Holding in Germany GmbH and Sasol
Limited would be jointly and severally be liable for EUR 250 million). The

fine is payable within three months.

As a result of Sasol's co-operation and support in the investigations, the

European  Commission reduced the base amount of the fine by 50% to the net

amount stated above.


Page 54 of 191 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
Sasol is surprised by and does not understand the reasons for the magnitude of
this fine and will be studying the reasons for the finding with a view to lodge an appeal against it.
According to the statement of objections of the European  Commission an infringement of antitrust laws commenced in 1992 or even earlier. In 1995
Sasol became a co-shareholder in an existing wax business located in Hamburg, Germany owned by the Schumann group.  In July 2002 Sasol acquired the remaining shares in the joint venture and became the sole shareholder of the
business. Sasol Limited was unaware of these infringements before the

European  Commission commenced their investigation at the wax business in

Hamburg in April 2005.

Sasol views this matter in a serious light and has intensified its competition
and anti-trust law compliance programmes in all its businesses including joint
ventures. It is Sasol's policy to comply with all applicable laws, including competition laws.

HD       EU fines Total 128 mln euros for price-fixing
WC       205 words
PD        1 October 2008
ET        11:16 AM
SN        Reuters News
SC        LBA
LA        English
CY        (c) 2008 Reuters Limited

PARIS, Oct 1 (Reuters) - Total has been fined about 128 million  euros ($181 million) by the  European
Commission for fixing prices of paraffin  wax, the French oil company said on Wednesday.

A Total spokeswoman said the company's French division was one of nine accused of fixing the price of the wax used for candles and  waxed paper between 1992 and 2005.

TD
The Commission also fined South Africa's Sasol and Italy's Eni but the spokeswoman did not specify how much. Royal Dutch Shell was not  fined, she added.

The European Commission had informed Total of its decision on Wednesday, Total said, but it had yet to receive the supporting arguments.

"Total will examine the supporting arguments of the judgment and examine the means of appeal," the spokeswoman said. Total received notification in 2007 of the claim that nine companies had exchanged confidential information concerning  paraffin wax.

Shares in Total, the world's fourth largest company, were little changed at 42.5  euros by 0853 GMT. (Reporting by Vanessa Walters and Benjamin Mallet; Editing by Paul Bolding)

HD      UPDATE 4-EU fines "paraffin mafia"  wax makers' cartel
BY      By Paul Taylor
WC     582 words
PD      1 October 2008
ET      11:39 AM
SN      Reuters News
SC      LBA
LA       English
CY      (c) 2008 Reuters Limited

LP
(Adds ENI reaction, para 12)

BRUSSELS, Oct 1 (Reuters) - The European Commission fined nine petrochemicals companies a total of 676 million euros ($955 million) on Wednesday for forming a "paraffin  mafia" to fix prices and carve
up markets for paraffin  wax.

TD
"There is probably not a household or company in  Europe that has not bought products affected by this
'paraffin  mafia'  cartel, with all that implies in terms of paying over the odds, higher costs and economic
damage," EU Competition Commissioner Neelie Kroes said.

Paraffin waxes are used in a wide range of products from candles to paper cups and plates, the  wax
coating of cheese, chemicals, tyres and chewing gum.

The biggest individual  fine of 318.2 million  euros was imposed on Sasol of South Africa and Germany, which the European Union executive described as the leader of the illegal  cartel, an official statement said.

Anglo-Dutch oil major Shell escaped a potential  fine of 96 million euros because it blew the whistle first to the EU competition authorities.

Kroes said the  cartel was known inside Shell as the "paraffin  mafia" and in Sasol as "Blauer Saloon" (Blue Saloon) after the hotel bar in Hamburg, Germany, where the first meetings of executives from the companies were held.

It was a very serious infringement of EU treaty antitrust rules, compounded by the duration of the  cartel, she said.

It was the fourth-highest  fine ever imposed by EU regulators on a sector, topped only by the record 992.3 million euros on elevator companies last year, 790.5 million on makers of vitamins in 2001 and 750.5 million on manufacturers of gas insulated switchgear in 2007.
SASOL APPEAL
Sasol, the world's biggest maker of motor fuel from coal, said it would likely appeal the ruling.

"Sasol is surprised by and does not understand the reasons for the magnitude of this  fine and will be studying the reasons for the finding with a view to lodge an appeal against it," the company said in a statement.

The other companies  fined were Total (128.1 million), Exxon Mobil (83.6 million  euros), RWE (37.4 million), ENI (29 million), Hansen & Rosenthal <24 million), MOL (23.7 million), Repsol (19.8 million), and Tudapetrol (12 million).

Eni said it would appeal, adding it noted "the  Commission has estimated the company's involvement ... as marginal and limited in time (2002-2005)."

Page 58 of 191 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
The Commission said the cartel activity took place between 1992 and 2005, when it began investigating with raids on petrochemicals companies prompted by an application from Shell for leniency in return for information provided.
The companies were well aware their activity was illegal, Kroes added.

"I sincerely hope... that these high  fines will encourage the management of these companies and others to look very carefully at what their staff are doing, and I hope that in turn the shareholders... will look very carefully at the management," she said.

THe Commission said individuals or companies that were victims of the  cartel were entitled to seek damages in national courts of EU member states. See related factbox [nL1211812] (Additional reporting by Jeremy Smith, Ingrid Melander and James Macharia in Johannesburg, Svetlana Kovalyova in Milan; Editing by Dale Hudson, Richard Hubbard and Jon Loades-Carter)

HD       EU Fines Sasol R3,7 Billion Over 'Paraffin  Mafia' BY        by Siseko Njobeni
WC      706 words
PD       2 October 2008
ET        11:05 AM SN       All Africa SC       AFNWS LA        English
CY       (c) 2008 AllAfrica, All Rights Reserved

LP
Johannesburg, Oct 02, 2008 (Business Day/All Africa Global Media via COMTEX) -- THE  European      Commission yesterday slapped a EUR 318,2m (R3,7bn) fine on Sasol for its role as a leader of a
price-fixing "paraffin  mafia" cartel that operated in the European paraffin  wax market for 13 years.
The cartel of nine was jointly  fined EUR 676m, and Sasol's penalty was the largest.

TD
The commission started investigating the  cartel in 2005 when one of the members, oil multinational
Shell, blew the whistle on the companies' activities in return for immunity from a EUR 96m  fine.
"Shell was the first company to inform us about the  cartel," European Competition Policy Commissioner
Neelie Kroes said yesterday. 96m  fine.
The EUR 318,2m, the biggest antitrust  fine imposed on a South African company and which Sasol said
it might appeal against, dwarfs the punishment meted out to the other members of the  cartel. Kroes said
this was because of the role Sasol played as leader of the  cartel. The fine is payable in three months.
Sasol's financial statements for the year to June showed it had R4,3bn in cash and cash equivalents.

The other  cartel members are: Total (France,  fined EUR 128m), Exxon Mobil (US, EUR 83m), Repsol, (Spain, EUR 20m), Tudapetrol (Germany, EUR 12m), Hansen and Rosenthal (Germany, EUR 24m), RWE (Germany, EUR 37m) and MOL (Hungary, EUR 23m).

The EUR 676m  fine is the fourth-highest yet imposed by the  commission. Kroes said the penalty was a reflection of the duration of the  cartel and the size of the affected market, which was worth almost EUR
500m a year.

"There is probably not a household or a company in  Europe that has not bought products affected by this cartel," she said.

Kroes said in a hard-hitting statement that the  cartel's meetings took place at top hotels in Milan, Vienna, Paris, Munich and Strasbourg. Kroes said companies participating in the  cartel knew what they were doing, and that it was wrong.

This was not Sasol's first brush with competition authorities. In May 2005, SA's Competition Commission found that Sasol Chemicals and two other companies, Kynoch and Omnia Fertiliser, had fixed fertiliser prices. The matter has since been referred to the Competition Tribunal.

Sasol spokeswoman Jacqui O'Sullivan said yesterday the group was surprised, did not understand the reasons for the magnitude of the  fine, and would be "studying the reasons for the finding with a view to lodging an appeal against it".
O'Sullivan said the group was not aware of the infringements before the start of the probe in April 2005. But analyst Paul Theron of stockbroking firm Vestact said an appeal might be ill-advised, given that the
fine was reduced by 50% for good behaviour.


Page 62 of 191 © 2019 Factiva, Inc. All rights  reserved.
He said news of the  fine coincided with a recovery in Sasol's share price after Monday's sell-off. "Before the news of the  fine broke, the share was trading at R363,63. It fell about R10 per share, but has recovered a bit since then."

Theron said that had it not been for the news of the  fine, Sasol's share price might have recovered more.
Sasol fell 5,12% on the JSE yesterday and it was R332 at the close.

Paraffin wax is used in a wide range of products, including tyres, car components,  waxed paper, paper cups and plates, packaging, chewing gum,  wax coating on cheese, and candles.
The cartel covered 75% of the  European paraffin wax market.

"I hope that the harsh lesson of these high  fines will encourage the management of these companies to look very carefully at what their staff is doing. And I hope that in turn the shareholders of these companies look very carefully at the management," Kroes said.
The commission earlier this year ordered Microsoft to pay EUR 899m for not complying with terms of a
2004 ruling.

In 1995, three years after the apparent start of the anticompetitive behaviour, Sasol became a co-shareholder in a wax business in Hamburg, Germany, owned by the Schumann group.
In July 2002, Sasol acquired the remaining shares in the joint venture.

HD       Sasol's Image Hurt By Its R3,7 Billion Fix
BY        by Siseko Njobeni
WC       510 words
PD        2 October 2008
ET        11:06 AM SN        All Africa SC        AFNWS LA        English
CY        (c) 2008 AllAfrica, All Rights Reserved

LP
Johannesburg, Oct 02, 2008 (Business Day/All Africa Global Media via COMTEX) -- THE stink that goes with being branded a price fixer may give Sasol a bigger hangover than the EUR 318,2m (R3,7bn)  fine imposed by the European Commission for its role in the "paraffin  Mafia".
Sasol and other groups, including Exxon Mobil, Total Respsol, Tudapetrol, Hansen & Rosenthal, RWE
and MOL, find themselves in the  commission's firing line.

TD
Their sin? From 1992 to 2005, representatives of these companies, excluding Sasol, which joined the cartel only when it became a shareholder in a German  wax business owned by the Schumann group three years later, met at top  European hotels and hatched plans to fix prices and share markets for the sale of paraffin wax. And they were not small-time players.

The companies, which called themselves "the blue saloon group", accounted for 75% of the  European  paraffin wax market. Paraffin wax is used in tyres, car parts,  waxed paper, paper cups and plates, chewing gum and candles.

The commission imposed a fine of EUR 676m (R7,9bn) on the companies, the fourth-largest  fine it has imposed to date. It said Sasol was not just an obscure member of the  cartel but took a leading role. For this reason, the EC saw fit to make Sasol's  fine heavier at EUR 318,2m.

Sasol said it would study the ruling and consider appealing. But a Cape Town analyst said Sasol should just pay the  fine and move on. "Their cash flows are more than enough to pay it."

Warwick Lucas of Imara SP Reid agreed. The  fine was about 11% of profits, so Sasol could pay it. "It should not damage their project pipeline."

Bearing the financial burden should be easier than shaking off a tag as a price fixer. Just look at the number of times Tiger Brands and  price fixing  have been mentioned in the same breath in the past year.

Sasol must now embark on the long journey to win back public confidence and mend the harm to its reputation. This seems to have started in earnest.

The group said, "Sasol views this matter in a serious light and has intensified its competition and antitrust law compliance programmes in all its businesses, including joint ventures. It is Sasol's policy to comply with all applicable laws, including competition law."

Yesterday started with much promise for Sasol. At one stage its share price on the JSE was R363,63, but it tumbled 4,54% to R334 at the close. Sasol admitted it was taken aback at the size of the  fine. It expected less, having been the second company, after Shell, to offer full co-operation.
The chronology of events raises questions. Sasol became a shareholder in the German  wax business in
1995 and got full ownership in 2002. The EC says the price fixing  started in 1992. So what happens to
the previous shareholders under whose watch the price fixing  started?

| nfcpin : FC&E Industry News Filter

HD     (EU) EU/COMPETITION: “Paraffin mafia” heavily fined
WC    547 words
PD     2 October 2008
SN     Agence Europe
SC     AGEU
LA     English
CY     Not Available for Re-Dissemination, except as permitted by your subscriber agreement. (c) Agence
Europe, Brussels 2008. All rights reserved.

LP
Brussels, 01/10/2008 (Agence  Europe) - On Wednesday 1 October, the  European Commission imposed a total of €676,011,400  fines on 9 groups - ENI, ExxonMobil, Hansen & Rosenthal, Tudapetrol, MOL, Repsol, Sasol, RWE and Total - for participating in a  cartel for paraffin  wax in the European Economic Area (EEA) between 1992 and 2005. Shell also participated in the cartel but was not fined because it revealed the existence of the  cartel to the Commission. The infringement committed by ExxonMobil, Sasol, Shell, RWE and Total also related to slack wax sold to end-customers on the German market.
Slack wax is the raw material used to produce paraffin  wax. All participants fixed prices for the products concerned.

TD
ExxonMobil, MOL, Repsol, Sasol, Shell and Total, in addition, allocated markets and customers for
paraffin waxes.
“There is probably not a household or company in  Europe that has not bought products affected by this
'paraffin  mafia' cartel, with all that implies in terms of paying over the odds, higher costs and economic
damage,” Competition Commissioner Neelie Kroes told press. Paraffin waxes are used in a wide variety
of products such as candles,  waxed paper, paper cups and plates, the wax coating on cheese, chemicals,
tyres and car components as well as in the rubber, packaging, adhesive and chewing gum industries.
Kroes estimated the value of the market at almost €500 million.

In the Shell group, the  cartel was called “paraffin  mafia” and in the Sasol group, “Blauer Salon” (“blue saloon”), after a hotel bar in Germany where the first meetings of the  cartel took place. Subsequent meetings took place at a series of top hotels all over  Europe, including Milan, Vienna, Budapest, Paris, Munich and Strasbourg. The cartel constituted a very serious infringement of EC Treaty antitrust rules, Kroes pointed out. In setting the fines (the fourth highest ever imposed by the  Commission), the Commission took into account the respective affected sales of the companies involved as well as the combined market share and the geographical scope of the cartel agreements. Sasol's  fine was increased by 50% because it was the leader of the cartel. The Commission increased the fines for ENI and Shell
by 60% because they had already been fined for cartel activities in previous Commission decisions, but
Shell was the first company to come forward with information about the cartel under the Commission's
2002 Leniency Notice and, therefore, received full immunity from  fines. The Commission, acting under its
leniency programme, also rewarded three groups for cooperating with the investigation. Sasol, Repsol and
ExxonMobil were granted a reduction of their  fines of 50%, 25% and 7% respectively.
In concrete terms, Shell has received a 100% reduction under the leniency programme (the €96 million
fine has been written off) and will not have to pay anything. Sasol has been  fined €318.2 million (including
reduction), Repsol €19.8 million (including reduction), ExxonMobil €83.58 million (including reduction), ENI
€29.12 million, Tudapetrol €12 million, Hansen & Rosenthal €24 million, MOL €23.7 million, RWE €37.44
million and Total €128.16 million.

The Commission points out that any person or company adversely affected by cartels can refer the case to member states' courts to seek damages. (O.L./transl.rt)

SASOL LTD ("SSL-N") - Statement Issued by Sasol Limited in Response to an Announcement - by the European Commission Statement issued by Sasol Limited, in response to an announcement by the European Commission regarding a finding of anti-competitive behaviour by Sasol  Wax GmbH and other members of the European paraffin  wax industry. As anticipated in several previous announcements
made by Sasol Limited, the European Union found that members of the European paraffin  wax industry, including Sasol Wax GmbH, formed a cartel and violated antitrust laws. A fine of EUR 318 200 000 was imposed by the European Commission on Sasol Wax GmbH (of which Sasol  Wax International AG, Sasol Holding in Germany GmbH and Sasol Limited would be jointly and severally be liable for EUR 250 million). The  fine is payable within three months.

TD
As a result of Sasol's co-operation and support in the investigations, the  European Commission reduced the base amount of the  fine by 50% to the net amount stated above. Sasol is surprised by and does not understand the reasons for the magnitude of this  fine and will be studying the reasons for the finding with
a view to lodge an appeal against it. According to the statement of objections of the  European                   Commission an infringement of antitrust laws commenced in 1992 or even earlier. In 1995 Sasol became a co-shareholder in an existing  wax business located in Hamburg, Germany owned by the Schumann group. In July 2002 Sasol acquired the remaining shares in the joint venture and became the sole shareholder of the business. Sasol Limited was unaware of these infringements before the  European       Commission commenced their investigation at the  wax business in Hamburg in April 2005. Sasol views this matter in a serious light and has intensified its competition and anti-trust law compliance programmes in all its businesses including joint ventures. It is Sasol's policy to comply with all applicable laws, including competition laws.
